## FAQ

<details>
<summary><strong>How often is this list updated?</strong></summary>

Once a day. A GitHub Action pulls new entry-level listings from Dreamwork's public API, which crawls company career pages directly (Greenhouse, Lever, Ashby, Workday, and others). Use <kbd>Ctrl</kbd>+<kbd>F</kbd> to search for backend, frontend, full-stack, mobile, embedded, DevOps, or security roles.

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>What counts as a new grad job here?</strong></summary>

Roles classified as junior in engineering, data, or security. Senior, staff, and management titles are filtered out, and so are internships, which have <a href="https://github.com/dreamworkhq/Tech-Internships-2026">their own list</a>. Most roles fit 2025 to 2027 graduates in CS and related fields.

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Where does the salary data come from?</strong></summary>

From the postings themselves. Many US listings disclose a range because of pay-transparency laws. When a posting does not state pay, the column is blank. Nothing is estimated.

</details>

<details>
<summary><strong>Can a tool apply to these for me?</strong></summary>

Yes. <a href="https://www.dreamworkhq.com/?utm_source=github&utm_medium=faq&utm_campaign=gh-new-grad-swe">Dreamwork</a> matches your resume against every listing here, tailors each application, and can submit them for you. Seeing your matches is free.

</details>

## How this list is built

A [GitHub Action](.github/workflows/update.yml) runs once a day. It queries Dreamwork's public listings API, filters for entry-level software engineering, data, and security roles in the United States, removes duplicates, and rewrites this README. The raw snapshot lives in [`data/listings.json`](data/listings.json). Listings are crawled directly from company career pages and ATS boards (Greenhouse, Lever, Ashby, Workday, and others), so links go to real, currently open postings. Found a bad listing? [Open an issue](../../issues).
